Other vertebrates noted: None.--This was a new transect that began at Davis Dam where the river cuts through bedrock and is deep and narrow. It continues south for 2 miles to Laughlin, NV. Throughout this section the river's western bank is composed of 20-30' high bluffs. The east bank is not as steeply or as deeply cut and has a few shoals and gravel bars extending out into the main channel somewhat at times of low water levels such as now. the water is apparently fairly dep here because the entire stretch is frequented by diving ducks - goldeneye, megansers, buffleheads. Redheads, scaup, and Ring-necked Ducks have been seen here previously.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS1050356360	2021-01-13 22:53:26.149515	666	species	Red-breasted Merganser	Mergus serrator			8			Male, Adult (3); Female, Adult (3)	United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031	US-NV_2211	15			Hidden Beach	L13254337	P	39.2219169	-119.9297413	2021-01-12	12:35:00	obsr275128	S79150571	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	28	0.161		1	1		0	1	1			3 were definitely adult males—very dark heads with thin plumes, white necks, rusty breasts, dark backs, and small white windows within the dark area behind breast (in swimming posture). I think the other 5 were all adult females, but I did not see them all well enough to rule out one or two being first-winter males. However, these female/immature males were all clearly Red-breasted Mergansers—in comparison to a nearby Common Merganser, they were all smaller and less robust-looking, had duller heads (not as rusty), "blurrier" transition between the head color and the pale neck color, thinner bills, and all had thin head plumes. The 8 Red-breasted Mergansers were all together on the lake, mostly swimming N, and synchronously diving. I counted them several times to make sure I had the right number. This is the largest number of Red-breasted Mergansers I have ever seen in Nevada at one time.
